GT Equivalence Verification (PO23)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `x*exp(-|x|)` — an odd function of x that decays exponentially
2. `log(|v| + 1)` — since v ≤ 0 on this domain, `|v| = -v`, so this is `log(-v + 1)` = `log(1 - v)`
3. `sin(t)` — simple sinusoidal in t

Let me analyze the key structural elements candidates need:

**For the x-dependence:** The GT has `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT equivalent to:
- `log(c*x² + 1)` — this is even in x, while `x*exp(-|x|)` is odd
- `x/(x² + 1)` — this is a rational function, not exponentially decaying
- `tanh(x)` — this saturates at ±1, while `x*exp(-|x|)` goes to 0

The combination `log(c*x² + 1) + x/(x² + 1)` could potentially approximate but NOT exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**For the v-dependence:** The GT has `log(|v| + 1) = log(1 - v)` (since v ≤ 0). This is NOT equivalent to:
- `v` (linear)
- `v*exp(c*t)` — has t-dependence mixed in
- `v/(c + x)` — has x-dependence mixed in
- `exp(c*v)` — exponential, not logarithmic

**For the t-dependence:** `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift. It is NOT equivalent to `t` (linear) or `log(c*t + 1)`.

**Critical observation:** The GT's v-dependence is `log(|v| + 1)` with NO x or t coupling. The GT's x-dependence is `x*exp(-|x|)` with NO v or t coupling. The GT's t-dependence is `sin(t)` with NO x or v coupling.

Looking through ALL candidates:
- Most candidates use `log(c*x² + 1)` and `x/(x²+1)` for x-dependence — these cannot exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- Many use `v*exp(c*t)` for v-dependence — this couples v and t, which the GT doesn't have (unless c=0, giving just `c*v`, which is NOT `log(1-v)`).
- Many use `v/(c+x)` — this couples v and x.
- Many use `c*t` or `log(c*t+1)` for t-dependence — neither is `sin(t)`.

No candidate has the correct basis function `x*exp(-|x|)`. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of `log(x²+1)`, `x/(x²+1)`, `tanh(x)`, `exp(cx)`, polynomials, or rational functions of x. These are linearly independent function classes.

Similarly, `log(|v|+1)` cannot be expressed as `v*exp(ct)` or `v/(c+x)` for any constants.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none of them contain the necessary basis function `x*exp(-|x|)`, and none can exactly match the GT.
